STAT 402

Description of the data

This data set is based on one-year vehicle insurance policies taken out in 2006 in Canada. The following variables are available to you in the file insurance.csv on the Blackboard. These are the variables in your data set. veh value: vehicle value in 10,000, clm: occurrence of claim (0=no, 1=yes), vehage : age of the vehicle (1 (youngest), 2, 3, 4)), gender: gender of driver (M or F), area: driver’s area of residence (A, B, C, D, E, F), age cat: driver’s age category (1 (youngest), 2, 3, 4))

ins <- read.csv("C:/Users/abhin/Downloads/insurance_sub.csv",header=T)

Using the logit model

The code below estimates a logistic regression model using the glm (generalized linear model) function. First, we convert claim to a factor to indicate that claim should be treated as a categorical variable.

ins$resp <- cbind(ins$clm)
model1<-glm(resp~veh_value+veh_age+exposure+veh_body+gender+area+agecat, 
              family=binomial(link=logit),data=ins)

Conclusion

Looking closely at summary(model1) we can conclude that following are significant

Exposure with Pr(>|z|) = <2e-16 veh_bodyUTE with Pr(>|z|) = 0.010668 agecat with Pr(>|z|) = 0.000125

Redefining vehicle value as a categorical covariate

ins$veh_value1 <- cut(ins$veh_value, c(0,2.5, 5.0, 7.5,10,12.5))

Model with new covariate
